    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="04dab1b83bfe4a349063ca718dc73388">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: 'bfe34207-5aad-4227-a0a2-053fe04dcda0'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

   <div class="abstract-group  metis-abstract">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" id="abstract-graphical-en">
         <h2 id="d28562500" class="article-section__header section__title graphical abstractlang_en graphical">Graphical Abstract</h2>
         <div class="graphical-abstract">
            <p>The intervalence charge transfer (IVCT) of manganese and iron to vanadium ions in the design of Prussian blue analogues (PBA) cathodes for SIBs is verified and series of novel V<sup>3+</sup>-substituted MnPBA are successfully prepared. The optimized Na<sub>1.2</sub>V<sub>0.63</sub>Mn<sub>0.58</sub>Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub> cathode demonstrates incredible rate capability (94.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 20 A g<sup>−1</sup>) and remarkable long-cycle stability, surpassing the majority of reported sodium-ion cathodes.
            </p><figure>
               <div class="center graphic__image"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/237a9dcf-6d1c-4a72-942d-77738222f5a1/anie202500254-toc-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/237a9dcf-6d1c-4a72-942d-77738222f5a1/anie202500254-toc-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/91c52cd3-6107-4747-9cc4-2474c6293b13/anie202500254-toc-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/237a9dcf-6d1c-4a72-942d-77738222f5a1/anie202500254-toc-0001-m.jpg" alt="Description unavailable" title="Description unavailable" loading="lazy"></picture></a><p class="caption-style"></p>
               </div>
            </figure>
            <p></p>
            </div>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d28562582" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>Mn<sup>3+</sup> (d<sup>4</sup>) in manganese-based Prussian blue analogues (MnPBA) exhibits intrinsic orbital degeneracy upon sodiation/desodiation, resulting in severe Jahn–Teller distortion, which usually causes rapid capacity decay and sluggish kinetics. Unfortunately, traditional modification strategies are insufficient for electronic tuning of Mn<sup>3+</sup> to mitigate these issues. Herein, Intervalence Charge Transfer (IVCT) of manganese and iron to vanadium ions is unraveled in a series of novel V<sup>3+</sup>-substituted MnPBA to enhance electrochemical reaction reversibility and kinetics. IVCT drives electron distribution from localized to delocalized, achieves electronic coupling, and mitigates Jahn–Teller by transferring a single-electron of Mn<sup>3+</sup> e<sub>g</sub> orbital. Notably, the reported Na<sub>1.2</sub>V<sub>0.63</sub>Mn<sub>0.58</sub>Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub> cathode demonstrates excellent rate capability (136.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 20 mA g<sup>−1</sup> and 94.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 20 A g<sup>−1</sup>), remarkable long-cycle stability (91.6 % capacity retention after 300 cycles at 20 mA g<sup>−1</sup> and 90.7 % after 2000 cycles at 2 A g<sup>−1</sup>), and robust performance across a wide temperature range (98.59 % capacity after 300 cycles at −30 °C and 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>), surpassing the majority of reported sodium-ion cathodes. The intrinsic functioning mechanism of IVCT and quasi-zero-strain reaction mechanism were adequately understood through systematic in situ/ex situ characterizations. This study further develops electron-tuning of PBA, opening a new avenue toward advanced sodium-ion battery cathode materials.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="anie202500254-sec-0001">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="anie202500254-sec-0001-title"> Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>The development and utilization of clean and sustainable energy have emerged as pressing priorities in recent years, which has intensified research efforts in the field of energy storage technologies.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0001_R_d28562467e463" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1">1</a></sup></span> Among the various energy storage systems, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered a promising alternative for grid-scale applications owing to a similar energy storage mechanism to lithium-ion batteries, abundant sodium resources, and low cost.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0005_R_d28562467e466" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2">2</a></sup></span> Since the cathode material directly determines the energy density and output voltage of battery chemistry, it is crucial to explore high-performance cathodes with stable and rapid Na<sup>+</sup> storage capabilities.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0010_R_d28562467e471" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3">3</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <p>Among various cathodes for SIBs, Prussian blue analogues (PBA), summarized by the formula A<sub>x</sub>M<sub>1</sub>[M<sub>2</sub>(CN)<sub>6</sub>]<sub>1-y</sub>□<sub>y</sub>⋅nH<sub>2</sub>O (0&lt;x≤2, 0≤y&lt;1), A: alkali metal ions, M<sub>1</sub>/M<sub>2</sub>: transition metal ions and □: [M<sub>2</sub>(CN)<sub>6</sub>] vacancies, are considered as promising candidates due to their open ionic diffusion pathways and tunable compositions.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0014_R_d28562467e500" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4">4</a></sup></span> A notable example is Na<sub>2</sub>Mn[Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub>] (MnPBA), which demonstrates great potential for application in Energy Storage Systems (ESSs) due to its low cost, high theoretical capacity (168 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> based on two sodium-ion storage), and high energy density equal to commercial LiFePO<sub>4</sub>.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0020_R_d28562467e511" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5">5</a></sup></span> However, the Mn<sup>3+</sup> has an intrinsic single-electron orbital degeneracy upon sodiation/desodiation, which leads to severe Jahn–Teller distortion, causing rapid capacity decay and sluggish kinetics.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0023_R_d28562467e517" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6">6</a></sup></span> Extensive efforts have been made to improve MnPBA cathode electrochemical performance, including constructing highly crystalline MnPBA,<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0027_R_d28562467e520" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7">7</a></sup></span> growing an extrinsic coating<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0018_R_d28562467e523" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4d - Angew. Chem. Int. Ed.">4d</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0021_R_d28562467e523" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5a - Angew. Chem. Int. Ed.">5a</a></sup></span> and doping the inert transition metal ions,<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0030_R_d28562467e526" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Mater.">8</a></sup></span> etc. While these strategies have enhanced their practical applications, they fail to resolve the intrinsic Jahn–Teller distortion of Mn<sup>3+</sup>, thereby rendering these improvements ineffective or negligible under conditions of high rate, low temperature, and prolonged cycling. From an analysis based solely on the electronic structure of the Mn valence shell, the suppression of this distortion could theoretically be achieved by: (1) constructing a system with low-spin Mn<sup>3+</sup> ions, (2) transferring the unpaired electron in the high-spin Mn<sup>3+</sup> e<sub>g</sub> orbital to reduce its orbital degeneracy.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0031_R_d28562467e538" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9">9</a></sup></span> The structural composition of MnPBA, where the M<sub>2</sub> site is characterized by low-spin Fe<sup>2+</sup> (low spin d<sup>6</sup>) and the M<sub>1</sub> site by high-spin Mn<sup>2+</sup> (high spin d<sup>5</sup>), makes the realization of the former strategy impractical.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0034_R_d28562467e554" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10">10</a></sup></span> In this way, it is crucial to adopt electronic tuning to mitigate the single electron on the Mn<sup>3+</sup> e<sub>g</sub> orbital to alleviate its Jahn–Teller effect. However, the basic understanding of the electron conduction mechanism within the framework of most PBA remains limited, which hinders the application of electronic tuning. Given the success of Intervalence Charge Transfer (IVCT) in explaining the electronic properties of many mixed valence coordination compounds, the introduction of IVCT for the electronic tuning of MnPBA, by leveraging the adjustable compositional advantages of PBA is crucial and ground-breaking.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0037_R_d28562467e562" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11">11</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <p>IVCT, a classic concept in chemistry, describes the electronic coupling between sites with different formal charges, leading to rapid charge oscillation.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0040_R_d28562467e567" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Inorg. Chem.">12</a></sup></span> Mixed-valence compounds comprise two or more electroactive moieties in more than one formal oxidation state. The degree of charge delocalization between two sites (A and B) is usually described by the classification Scheme proposed by Robin and Day. In Class II, the IVCT between A and B is accessible given the small optical or thermoelectric activation energy. Iron (II, III)-based PBA represents some of the earliest substances recognized as Class II compounds, with their coloration attributed to the presence of IVCT.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0038_R_d28562467e570" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11a - Chem. Rev.">11a</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0041_R_d28562467e570" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Chem. Soc. Rev.">13</a></sup></span> In MnPBA, the valence states of manganese and iron ions are equivalent, which hinders the occurrence of IVCT. The activation of the IVCT in MnPBA for electronic tuning can be accomplished by introducing heterovalent ions, characterized by an initial state greater than 2 and an oxidation state exceeding 3. The commonly discussed transition metal ions like Fe, Co, Ni, Cu, and Zn at the M<sub>1</sub> site do not fulfill the requirements. Therefore, we can only consider vanadium ions as a replacement for Mn<sup>2+</sup> to form V<sup>3+</sup>Mn<sup>2+</sup>PBA due to their diverse oxidation states and stable properties. (1) The initial IVCT between Mn<sup>2+</sup>-V<sup>3+</sup> and Fe<sup>2+</sup>-V<sup>3+</sup> allows for delocalized electron distribution.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0042_R_d28562467e590" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Inorg. Chem.">14</a></sup></span> Meanwhile, electronic coupling among different transition metal ions drives charge–discharge platform coupling. (2) Under high voltage, the IVCT between Mn<sup>3+</sup>-V<sup>4+</sup> reduces the single electron on Mn<sup>3+</sup> e<sub>g</sub> orbital, mitigating its strong Jahn–Teller distortion and thus ensuring long-term cycling stability. Therefore, a series of novel VMnPBA with varied V<sup>3+</sup> contents were prepared via a modified co-precipitation method which utilized ascorbic acid as a supportive additive. Most notably, the reported V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA cathode demonstrates excellent rate capability (136.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 20 mA g<sup>−1</sup> and 94.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 20 A g<sup>−1</sup>), remarkable long-cycle stability (91.6 % capacity retention after 300 cycles at 20 mA g<sup>−1</sup> and 90.7 % after 2000 cycles at 2 A g<sup>−1</sup>), and robust performance across a wide temperature range (98.59 % capacity after 300 cycles at −30 °C and 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>). The intrinsic functioning mechanisms of IVCT and quasi-zero-strain reaction mechanisms were adequately understood through systematic in situ/ex situ characterizations. Additionally, the V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA cathode was matched with the hard carbon (HC) anode to be reasonably assembled into a full cell, which exhibited promising application prospects. The study provides a promising innovative approach for the vast PBA family compounds with unique electronic conductivity mechanisms and synthetic flexibility.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="anie202500254-sec-0002">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="anie202500254-sec-0002-title"> Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <p>A series of novel V<sup>3+</sup>-substituted VMnPBA samples were synthesized through a modified co-precipitation method that innovatively incorporates ascorbic acid as an auxiliary additive for in situ reduction and chelation of the raw materials, which effectively reduces the local concentration of reactants and minimizes the occurrence of vacancy defects within the formed VMnPBA crystals (Figure S1, S2). The introduction of V<sup>3+</sup> activates the previously blocked IVCT in MnPBA, facilitating electrons transfer between the Mn<sup>2+</sup> and Fe<sup>2+</sup> sites with the V<sup>3+</sup> site in various charge states, which results in rapid charge oscillations among them. This process leads to the formation of characteristic absorption bands, as evidenced by Ultraviolet-Visible Diffuse Reflectance Spectroscopy (UV/Vis-DRS) that reveals broad characteristic absorption features within both the near-infrared (NIR) and visible regions of the spectrum (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0001">1a</a>).<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0038_R_d28562467e651" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11a - Chem. Rev.">11a</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0041_R_d28562467e651" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Chem. Soc. Rev.">13</a></sup></span> In the wavelength range of 190–1800 nm, at least four overlapping absorption bands are identified. In conjunction with previous studies, characteristic ligand-to-metal charge transfer (LMCT) and metal-to-ligand charge transfer (MLCT) absorption peaks have been observed in various PBA materials.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0043_R_d28562467e654" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15">15</a></sup></span> The absence of valence difference in MnPBA impedes IVCT between the transition metal ions, thereby no discernible IVCT absorption peak is observed. In addition, due to the complete filling of the t<sub>2g</sub> electron orbitals in low-spin Fe<sup>2+</sup>, weak MLCT was detected, resulting in a relative localization of electrons within the system. Following the introduction of V<sup>3+</sup>, two pronounced IVCT absorption peaks at 883 nm and 712 nm were detected, and the characteristic absorption peaks associated with LMCT and MLCT were significantly enhanced. This activation of electron transfer within the system facilitated electron distribution from localized to delocalized. The UV/Vis DRS exhibited an asymmetric peak profile, revealing two suitable IVCT bands. This observation suggests that VMnPBA aligns with the transition states of electron delocalization in both class 2 (semiconductor) and class 3 (metal) systems as classified by Robin-Day, which is consistent with previously reported isolated tri- and tetranuclear CN-bridged Ru complexes.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0037_R_d28562467e664" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11">11</a></sup></span> Furthermore, this IVCT feature absorption peak elucidates the intense coloration observed in the mixed-valent VMnPBA (Figure S3).<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0042_R_d28562467e667" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Inorg. Chem.">14</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0046_R_d28562467e667" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">16</a></sup></span> The intrinsic mechanism underlying the initial IVCT in VMnPBA can be further elucidated through high-resolution X-ray Photoelectron Spectroscopy (XPS) (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0001">1b</a> and Figure S4). The pronounced characteristic peaks corresponding to Mn<sup>2+</sup> 2p<sub>1/2</sub> (641.5 eV) and Mn<sup>3+</sup> 2p<sub>1/2</sub> (643.3 eV) observed in a series of VMnPBA samples indicate the two valencies of Mn ions. Meanwhile, the V 2p spectrum reveals the presence of V<sup>2+</sup> 2p<sub>1/2</sub> (515.3 eV) and V<sup>3+</sup> 2p<sub>1/2</sub> (516.5 eV). These findings could suggest that the substituted V<sup>3+</sup> facilitates IVCT from Mn<sup>2+</sup> to V<sup>3+</sup> within VMnPBA. It is worth noting that the feature peaks of Fe<sup>3+</sup> are less prominent in VMnPBA, which may be attributed to the stable electronic configuration of low-spin Fe<sup>2+</sup> (t<sub>2g</sub><sup>6</sup>e<sub>g</sub><sup>0</sup>) that inhibits IVCT from Fe<sup>2+</sup> to V<sup>3+</sup>. The weaker oxidation state ion peaks for Mn<sup>3+</sup> and Fe<sup>3+</sup> were also detected in MnPBA, potentially resulting from unavoidable oxidation during synthesis. The distinct peaks for single Fe<sup>2+</sup> 2p<sub>1/2</sub> (708.6 eV) and Fe<sup>2+</sup> 2p<sub>3/2</sub> (721.6 eV) in V<sub>0.20</sub>Mn<sub>0.80</sub>PBA substantiate the effectiveness of ascorbic acid-assisted reduction. Moreover, V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA demonstrates the most pronounced characteristic peaks of Mn<sup>3+</sup> and V<sup>2+</sup>, indicating the maximum occurrence of the IVCT, which aligns with the analysis results of UV/Vis-DRS detection.
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="anie202500254-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/c046ec8f-fc57-482c-a96a-9558496933c9/anie202500254-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/c046ec8f-fc57-482c-a96a-9558496933c9/anie202500254-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/e110e908-92cb-4922-bc39-7d14e3fdebf4/anie202500254-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/c046ec8f-fc57-482c-a96a-9558496933c9/anie202500254-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=anie202500254-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fanie.202500254" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>a) UV/Vis-DRS spectra of as-prepared samples. b) XPS spectra of as-prepared samples. The Rietveld refinement of XRD patterns of (c) MnPBA and (d) V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA. e) The EPR, f) FT-IR, and (g) Raman spectra of the four samples: MnPBA, V<sub>0.2</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>PBA, V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA, and V<sub>0.8</sub>Mn<sub>0.2</sub>PBA.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>The X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns obtained by Rietveld refinement on GSAS software (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0001">1c</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0001">1d</a>) toward the as-prepared VMnPBA samples are indexed as the typical cubic structures with the space group of Fm-3 m (Figure S5, S6), while MnPBA is indexed as the monoclinic structures with the space group of P21/n.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0047_R_d28562467e787" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17">17</a></sup></span> In addition, it is found that the gradually increased content of V<sup>3+</sup>, resulted in the progressively shifts of (200) peaks toward higher angles, which can be attributed to the incorporation of small-radius V<sup>3+</sup>, thereby indirectly validating the success of substitution. These transformations enable VMnPBA to exhibit lower structural strain, thereby contributing to its exceptional long-cycle stability. Comprehensive crystal data can be found in Tables S1–S3 of the Supporting Information. Meanwhile, corresponding diagrams of the crystal structures are also included. To ensure the integrity of the crystal structure and achieve superior electrochemical stability, it is essential to minimize inevitable crystalline water and vacancy defects within the PBA framework. By utilizing acid chelation-assistance route for in situ reduction, the electron paramagnetic resonance (EPR) curve of all the V<sup>3+</sup>-substituted MnPBA exhibit markedly diminished response peaks compared to that of MnPBA, indicating a reduced presence of vacancy defects in VMnPBA (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0001">1e</a>). Furthermore, the observed broadening of the EPR peak may be due to a delocalized coupled electron system present within this material.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0050_R_d28562467e800" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Light Sci. Appl.">18</a></sup></span> Due to the optimized synthetic method and minimal defects within V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA, thermogravimetry analysis (TGA) indicates that V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA contains less crystal water. The total water contents for V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA and MnPBA are measured at 12.80 wt % and 14.18 wt %, respectively (Figure S7). The reduced vacancy defects and lower water content significantly enhance the stability during the cycling of V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA, thereby improving its inherent safety in practical applications. Moreover, the chemical formulas of MnPBA and V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA have been determined as Na<sub>1.80</sub>MnFe(CN)<sub>6</sub> and Na<sub>1.20</sub>Mn<sub>0.58</sub>V<sub>0.63</sub>Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub> via inductively coupled plasma-mass spectrometry (ICP-MS) (Tables S4). Scanning Electron Microscope (SEM) and Transmission Electron Microscope (TEM) reveal that a series of VMnPBA composites comprise nanoparticles formed by secondary particle aggregation with an average diameter of less than 50 nm (Figure S8–S12), significantly smaller than the typical cubic MnPBA particles measured to be 3 μm (Figure S9). What is more, Figure S13 demonstrates that the Brunauer–Emmett–Teller (BET) specific surface area of V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA and MnPBA reaches 78.0 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>−1</sup> and 3.49 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>−1</sup>. The reduced particle size and enlarged specific surface area facilitate interaction between the material and the electrolyte, while simultaneously minimizing the diffusion pathway for Na<sup>+</sup>, thereby accelerating the kinetics of electrochemical reactions.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0051_R_d28562467e853" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19">19</a></sup></span> In addition, the high-resolution TEM image of V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA reveals uniform lattice stripes on the particle surface, with a measured lattice spacing of 0.23 nm corresponding to the (420) crystal planes (Figure S8b). Furthermore, based on the scanning TEM image and the accompanying energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDX) mapping for V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA, six elements are uniformly distributed throughout the structure, further validating both the successful synthesis and high purity of V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA sample (Figure S8c, S8d). These two prominent peaks observed in the Fourier transform infrared spectroscopy (FT-IR) of a series of PBA at 1618 and 2068 cm<sup>−1</sup> can be ascribed to the characteristic stretching vibrations of the O−H bond and C≡N bonds, respectively. This analyzes result confirms the presence of interstitial water and elucidates the distinctive crystal structure of PBA (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0001">1f</a>). The Raman peak at 2092 cm<sup>−1</sup> for MnPBA corresponds to the benting vibration of Fe<sup>2+</sup>−C≡N, while the peak at 2130 cm<sup>−1</sup> is associated with both benting and stretching vibrations of M<sub>1</sub>−N≡C (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0001">1g</a>). Remarkably, the Raman peaks for the CN<sup>−</sup>-ligand of VMnPBA series exhibit coupling effects and a blue shift towards higher wavenumbers, indicating the enhanced stability of the C≡N bonds, which may be ascribed to the electronic system coupling induced by IVCT.</p>
         
         <p>The CV curves of the V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA and MnPBA samples were compared at a scan rate of 0.1 mV/s to elucidate the impact of IVCT, as illustrated in Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0002">2a</a>. Two distinct pairs of redox couples were identified for MnPBA at approximately 3.45/3.11 V and 3.80/3.58 V, which correspond to the transitions between high-spin Mn<sup>2+</sup>/Mn<sup>3+</sup> and low-spin Fe<sup>2+</sup>/Fe<sup>3+</sup>. The introduction of V<sup>3+</sup> leads to a notable broadening of the oxidation-reduction peaks for V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA at 3.49/3.20 V, which suggests a coupling between the high-spin Mn<sup>2+</sup>/Mn<sup>3+</sup> and V<sup>3+</sup>/V<sup>4+</sup> redox peaks, as well as the merging with Fe<sup>2+</sup>/Fe<sup>3+</sup> redox peaks into a single peak, which is attributed to electronic interactions induced by IVCT between (Mn<sup>2+</sup>-V<sup>3+</sup>) and (Fe<sup>2+</sup>-V<sup>3+</sup>). Particularly, the polarization of the coupled V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA oxidation-reduction peaks is considerably less than uncoupled MnPBA, and its electrochemical behavior remains largely unchanged during the initial four cycles compared to irreversible MnPBA CV curves. Similarly, the electrochemical coupling behavior is also evident in the charge–discharge curves of the VMnPBA series (Figure S14). At 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, the dQ/dV profiles for the first 50 cycles of MnPBA and V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA further substantiate the enhanced cycling stability associated with their coupled oxidation-reduction peaks (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0002">2b</a>,<a href="#anie202500254-fig-0002">2c</a>). The peaks in dQ/dV profiles corresponding to the coupled redox processes of V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA exhibit nearly unchanged contributions, achieving a capacity retention rate of 98.2 %, in contrast to that of MnPBA retention rate of only 67.2 % (Figure S15). After certain cycles, MnPBA also demonstrates similar coupled redox peak characteristics, which are reportedly attributed to the electrolysis of water due to the reduction in ligand field stabilization energy (LFSE), as reported.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0018_R_d28562467e957" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4d - Angew. Chem. Int. Ed.">4d</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0054_R_d28562467e957" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20">20</a></sup></span> However, while the coupling between Mn<sup>2+</sup>-N/Mn<sup>3+</sup>-N and Fe<sup>2+</sup>-C/Fe<sup>3+</sup>-C is frequently limited within the initial four cycles, subsequent cycling does display coupled electrochemical behavior. Nevertheless, intrinsic issues within MnPBA lead to a rapid decay in its differential capacity contribution peaks, indicating that it exhibits precarious electrochemical cycling stability. These significant problems include the dissolution of manganese ions induced by the significant Jahn–Teller distortion, substantial structural distortion, and strain deformation inherent to the monoclinic phase upon sodiation/desodiation, as well as the cyclical expansion and contraction of the crystal lattice over prolonged cycling, which ultimately results in macroscopic material fractures and compromised particles (Figure S16a). On the one hand, the above issues initiate a cascade of detrimental effects on the MnPBA cathode material, resulting in structural degradation and accelerated capacity loss (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0002">2e</a>). On the other hand, deposited manganese ions on the surface impede sodium ion migration, thereby diminishing its electrochemical kinetics. The aforementioned issues are mitigated in V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA, which has a stable electrochemical coupling platform. Simultaneously, the IVCT of Mn<sup>3+</sup>-V<sup>4+</sup> at upper voltages diminished the single electron on the e<sub>g</sub> orbital of Mn<sup>3+</sup>, thereby reducing its Jahn–Teller distortion. Besides, its intrinsic cubic phase exhibited a weaker phase transition during cycling (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0002">2f</a>). The obtained macroscopic bulk V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA materials composed of secondary nanoscale particles with low strain also remained intact throughout cycling, which might be favorable for the excellent long-term cycling stability of the electrode (Figure S16b).
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="anie202500254-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/967a9559-a276-4bde-be5e-2f4f3a79dfaa/anie202500254-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/967a9559-a276-4bde-be5e-2f4f3a79dfaa/anie202500254-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/434a4c73-af19-4042-b82d-73c4ad2f5fc9/anie202500254-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/967a9559-a276-4bde-be5e-2f4f3a79dfaa/anie202500254-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=anie202500254-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fanie.202500254" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>IVCT for enhanced electrochemical reversibility. a) Cyclic voltammograms (CV) curves at 0.1 mV/s. dQ/dV profiles of charge and discharge processes at the first 50 cycles of (b) V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA and (c) MnPBA. d) Cycling stability in 20 mA g<sup>−1</sup> and 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>. Scheme of (e) possible structural problems in MnPBA and (f) modification strategies in V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA. f) Cycling stability in 500 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, 1000 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, 2000 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, and (g) rate performance of MnPBA and V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>Rate capability and cycling experiments were conducted to exploit the advantageous effects of IVCT in enhancing the long-term reversibility and electrochemical kinetics of the material (Figure S17–S26). All the modified VMnPBA cathodes show improved long cycling and rate capabilities, especially for V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA, which demonstrated exceptional capacity retention rates of 91.6 % and 85.4 % after 300 and 650 cycles at 20 mA g<sup>−1</sup> and 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, much larger than MnPBA (30.6 % and 42.9 %) (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0002">2d</a> and Figure S17). The positive effect of IVCT on V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA was further demonstrated under higher current densities. As illustrated in Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0002">2g</a>, V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA demonstrated exceptional cycling performance over 500, 1000, and even up to 2000 cycles at current densities of 500, 1000, and 2000 mA g<sup>−1</sup> respectively, achieving impressive capacity retention rates of 90.5 %, 90.2 %, and 90.7 %, respectively. However, the capacity retention rates of MnPBA were notably low at 37.9 %, 37.0 %, and 38.2 %. The V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA exhibits excellent cycle stability even under high mass loading (Figure S19). The relatively low initial coulombic efficiency in V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA and MnPBA cathodes may be ascribed to the decomposition of electrolytes, SEI formation, and activation in the charging process. At an exceptionally high rate of 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA demonstrates an extraordinary cycle life exceeding 100,000 cycles (Figure S20 and Figure S21). The fluctuations in coulombic efficiency at elevated current densities are linked to electrochemical over-charging and over-discharging. Moreover, the internal IVCT facilitates the coupling of electrons within the PBA system, enabling a transition from localized to delocalized electron states and thereby enhancing its electrochemical kinetics (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0003">3</a>). Consequently, all optimized VMnPBA cathodes exhibit superior rate capabilities (Figure S22–26). Among them, V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA delivers admirable discharge capacities of 136.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 20 mA g<sup>−1</sup> and 94.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> even at 20 A g<sup>−1</sup>, which means this electrode material could be fully charged/discharged within 34 seconds (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0002">2h</a>). The data presented in Figures <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0002">2</a>(f, g) further emphasize that the V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA cathode has prominent rate capability<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0025_R_d28562467e1110" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6b - Angew. Chem. Int. Ed.">6b</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0026_R_d28562467e1110" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6c - Energy Storage Mater.">6c</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0057_R_d28562467e1110" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21">21</a></sup></span> and long-term cycling performance<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0021_R_d28562467e1113" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5a - Angew. Chem. Int. Ed.">5a</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0026_R_d28562467e1113" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6c - Energy Storage Mater.">6c</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0058_R_d28562467e1113" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21a - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">21a</a>-<a href="#anie202500254-bib-0061" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0061_R_d28562467e1113" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21d - Adv. Mater.">21d</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-bib-0065" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0065_R_d28562467e1113" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22">22</a></sup></span> even compared to the state-of-the-art SIBs cathode materials due to the occurrence of IVCT.
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="anie202500254-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/221efe3d-715b-4188-8248-ad28088b3265/anie202500254-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/221efe3d-715b-4188-8248-ad28088b3265/anie202500254-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/cdf7871f-9aac-4fa0-a377-787b17b98e00/anie202500254-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/221efe3d-715b-4188-8248-ad28088b3265/anie202500254-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=anie202500254-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fanie.202500254" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>IVCT for the enhanced kinetics. a) Comparison of intrinsic conductivity of MnPBA and VMnPBA series. b) GITT curves and the calculated <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/a728601a-35d3-4886-a9e9-7ec0043d7686/anie202500254-math-0001.png"></span><math></math>
. c) Linear fitting Randles–Sevcik curves between the maximum current and the square root of the scan rate for V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA and MnPBA electrodes. d) Arrhenius plots and the corresponding activation energy of V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA and MnPBA electrodes from different temperature EIS. DRT analysis based on the in situ EIS of (e)V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA and (f)MnPBA sample half battery. The partial density of states of (g) V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA and (h) Mn-PBA. The Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion barriers of (i) MnPBA and (j) V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA. The related scheme of three-dimensional Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion paths of (k) MnPBA and (l) V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>Compared to the more confined electron system within MnPBA, the optimized VMnPBA compounds demonstrate markedly enhanced intrinsic conductivity. As depicted in Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0003">3a</a>, the intrinsic conductivities of MnPBA and V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA, as determined by the four-probe method, are 4.26×10<sup>−3</sup> S/m and 9.68×10<sup>−3</sup> S/m, respectively. This enhancement in conductivity is beneficial for their charge–discharge performance at high rates. The apparent Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient (<span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/2e494054-4ffc-480e-9caa-6647da57cba0/anie202500254-math-0002.png"></span><math></math>
) was determined and calculated using the galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0003">3b</a> and Figure S27). The V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA sample exhibited <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/2c6287ca-d3ad-4f4a-bced-3ccd4b26ca2d/anie202500254-math-0003.png"></span><math></math>
 values fluctuating within the ranges of 10<sup>−9</sup> to 10<sup>−11</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>, while MnPBA displayed values ranging from 10<sup>−10</sup> to 10<sup>−14</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>. The higher <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/dad7c548-f011-42b6-a928-8a0a95f6c244/anie202500254-math-0004.png"></span><math></math>
 value suggests the reduced sodium diffusion barrier in V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA. Besides, the significant fluctuations in <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/4a665f0a-88e1-4057-8072-d6c4fac95e64/anie202500254-math-0005.png"></span><math></math>
 observed at the high voltage platform of MnPBA may be associated with its pronounced structural distortion, which impedes Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion. It should be highlighted that the GITT results align with <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/196eda0d-6d37-479c-9ef7-a7b9f7a9a0b1/anie202500254-math-0006.png"></span><math></math>
 fitted at different peak currents via the CV tests at different scan rates (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0003">3c</a>). The CV curve for the V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA exhibits reduced polarization and a more significant contribution from the diffusion-controlled process (Figure S28), indicating a marked improvement in its Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction efficiency. Subsequent variable-temperature impedance experiments were performed, and the charge-transfer activation energies (<i>E</i><sub>a</sub>) were determined using the Arrhenius equation (Figure S29). The <i>E</i><sub>a</sub> value for V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA (45.06 kJ mol<sup>−1</sup>) is markedly lower than that of MnPBA (65.51 kJ mol<sup>−1</sup>), indicating that V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA demonstrates enhanced charge-transfer kinetics (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0003">3d</a>). The analysis results of the in situ galvanostatic electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) combined with the distribution of relaxation time (DRT) elucidate the internal state and charge transfer dynamics of the material (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0003">3e</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0003">f</a> and Figure S30–S32). The reliability of the EIS data has been validated using the open “LIN-KK” tool for the Kramers-Kronig validity test. (Figure S31).<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0068" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0068_R_d28562467e1359" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23">23</a></sup></span> The distribution of relaxation time constants (τ) is connected to different processes of the research system. The peaks locate at τ<sub>1</sub> (−5.25 ~ −4.75), τ<sub>2</sub> (−3.5 ~ −1.5), τ<sub>3</sub> (−1 ~ 0), and τ<sub>4</sub> (0 ~ 2) correspond to internal resistance (R<sup>’</sup>), Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion process at the cathode-electrolyte interface (R<sub>CEI</sub>), charge transfer in electrodes (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) and solid-state diffusion (W<sub>diff</sub>), respectively, which are consistent with that of the previous report.<span><sup><a href="#anie202500254-bib-0071" class="bibLink tab-link" id="anie202500254-bib-0071_R_d28562467e1382" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Angew. Chem. Int. Ed.">24</a></sup></span> The V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA electrode overall exhibits reduced values of R<sup>’</sup>, R<sub>CEI</sub>, <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>, and W<sub>diff</sub> throughout the cycle compared to that of the MnPBA electrode, indicating superior electronic conductivity and faster electrochemical reaction kinetics for the V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA cathode (Figures S32). The R<sub>CEI</sub> peak for MnPBA is significantly higher than that of V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA, potentially resulting from the deposition of dissolved manganese ions at the interface. It is worth noting that the W<sub>diff</sub> peak position of V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA is almost unchanged compared with the markedly shifted W<sub>diff</sub> peak position of MnPBA after the complete cycle, which may indicate an irreversible phase transition process occurred for the MnPBA. Furthermore, a series of VMnPBA electrodes exhibit a lower resistance compared to the MnPBA electrode at the same number of cycles, thereby&nbsp;indicating the rapid electrode electrochemical reaction kinetics (Figure S33). To further assess the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics in the PBA framework that contribute to outstanding performance, density functional theory (DFT) calculations were conducted. The partial density of states (pDOS) curve indicates that V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA is a metallic compound exhibiting superior intrinsic electronic conductivity compared to MnPBA, as evidenced by the substantial electron density near the Fermi level resulting from electronic exchange via IVCT (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0003">3g</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0003">3h</a>). The enhanced conductivity of V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA facilitates improved kinetics for the Na<sup>+</sup> storage reaction during cycling, as illustrated in Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0003">3i</a>-<a href="#anie202500254-fig-0003">3l</a>. The calculated result of the three-dimensional Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion pathways reveals that the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion energy barrier for V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA is lower, thereby indicating faster Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion.</p>
         
         <p>The in situ Raman spectroscopy was employed to investigate the variations in the vibrational stretching of Fe−C≡NTM<sub>1</sub> during the insertion and extraction of Na<sup>+</sup> (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0004">4a</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0004">4b</a>, and Figure S34). In addition, the characteristic Raman peaks of both the original MnPBA and V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA electrodes aligned with the above-discussed Raman spectrum measurement result of MnPBA and V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA powders. During the charging and discharging, the chemical environment surrounding the C≡N in MnPBA experiences a significant transformation, characterized by the disappearance of two prominent Raman peaks correlated with the ν(Fe−C≡N−Mn) band and the emergence of a new peak at 2167 cm<sup>−1</sup>. Although this alteration is reversible, it also indicates substantial distortion within Fe−C≡N−Mn. In V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA, the intersite coupling induced by IVCT and a shrunken crystal structure is favorable for the higher stable Fe−C≡NTM<sub>1</sub> bond in V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA (only a reversible minor Raman blue shift) than that of MnPBA observed in the Raman spectrum, indicates minimal chemical bond distortion upon sodiation/desodiation of the V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA, which is believed to be responsible for the remarkable long-cycle stability of the electrode.
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="anie202500254-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/2bfd0d33-3b5d-4d16-96b3-7b4e4cd2addc/anie202500254-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/2bfd0d33-3b5d-4d16-96b3-7b4e4cd2addc/anie202500254-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/f00e7c37-3916-4d7f-92a5-71eebdb12908/anie202500254-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/2bfd0d33-3b5d-4d16-96b3-7b4e4cd2addc/anie202500254-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=anie202500254-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fanie.202500254" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>Sodium-ion storage mechanism. In situ Raman spectra of (a) MnPBA and (b)V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA. Intensity contour maps of (c)MnPBA and (d) V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA collected by in situ XRD. The corresponding galvanostatic charge–discharge voltage profiles at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup> and changes of the lattice parameter of (e) MnPBA and (f)V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA calculated from XRD results. The corresponding phase transition scheme of (g) MnPBA and (h)V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA. Ex situ XRD patterns of the (i) MnPBA and (j) V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA electrode before and after various cycling at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>. k) Ex situ XPS spectra of V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>To gain deeper insights into the structural stability of MnPBA and V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA upon the Na<sup>+</sup> first (de)insertion, in situ XRD techniques were employed to investigate the structural evolution (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0004">4c</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0004">4d</a>). At the initial charging process, MnPBA displayed a characteristic monoclinic structure. Particularly, the (220)/(024) peaks at ~24° merged into a single peak at 23.8° as the voltage increased from 1.6 to 3.5 V. In addition, the peak at 16.9° shifted towards lower angles, indicating a slight expansion of the unit cell that corresponds to a structural phase transition from monoclinic to cubic (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0004">4g</a>). In the following charging between 3.5 and 3.8 V, characteristic peaks exhibited minor shifts towards lower angles. During the later charging stage from 3.8 to 4.0 V, the peak at 16.8° significantly shifted to a higher angle, while the crystallinity slightly decreased, indicative of a second phase transition of MnPBA from cubic to tetragonal structure, wherein the unit cell underwent substantial contraction due to the extraction of a second Na<sup>+</sup>. During discharge, a reversible opposite trend is observed. However, the crystallinity of MnPBA exhibits a slight decrease following the initial cycle. V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA experiences a minimal phase transition between cubic and tetragonal structures during charging and discharging processes (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0004">4d</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0004">4h</a>), demonstrating a quasi-zero-strain reaction mechanism (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0004">4e</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0004">4f</a>). The structural stability of the V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA cathode has been significantly optimized. The ex situ XRD analysis of electrodes subjected to varied cycling numbers at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup> was conducted (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0004">4i</a>, <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0004">4j</a>). After the battery that composed of V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA electrode was cycled over 100 cycles, there are no significant phase transitions can be observed, indicating its excellent stability. In contrast, obvious structural degradation and reduced crystallinity occurred for MnPBA electrode.</p>
         
         <p>Ex situ XPS was employed to understand the intrinsic IVCT mechanism within V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA at several critical charge/discharge states (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0004">4k</a>). At the open circuit voltage (OCV), all metal ions in the electrode exhibit two valent characteristics due to the activation of IVCT (Mn<sup>2+</sup>- V<sup>3+</sup> and Fe<sup>2+</sup>-V<sup>3+</sup>), which aligns with the previously mentioned powder XPS results. As the voltage charges to 3.5 V, increased peaks corresponding to Mn<sup>3+</sup> are observed at 643.3 eV (2p<sub>1/2</sub>) and 655.5 eV (2p<sub>3/2</sub>) in the Mn 2p region. Notably, high-energy Mn<sup>3+</sup> peaks emerge that correspond to predicted IVCT between Mn<sup>3+</sup> and V<sup>4+</sup> at elevated voltages, leading to a reduction in singly occupied electrons in the e<sub>g</sub> orbital of Mn<sup>3+</sup>, thereby diminishing the Jahn–Teller effect. When charged to 4.0 V, Mn 2p and Fe 2p characteristic peaks shift towards higher binding energies, indicating further desodiation. Simultaneously, high-valent iron and manganese ion peaks appear alongside an increase in abnormal V<sup>3+</sup> peak area at high voltage, indicating intrinsic IVCT occurrence. During discharging, as the voltage falls below the OCV, characteristic peaks slightly shift toward lower binding energies while low-valent metal ion peak areas experience a slight increase compared to their initial condition. However, internal IVCT remains effective with all transition metal ions continuing to display two valent characteristics, which can be concluded that the IVCT in V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA possesses a high reversibility.</p>
         
         <p>Based on the preceding analysis, the IVCT diagram in both the initial and high voltage states is illustrated in Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0005">5a</a>, which effectively depicts the electron transfer from low-valent to high-valent cations within the mixed-valent VMnPBA, achieving their electron coupling. Furthermore, the thermal stability of IVCT was assessed via in situ variable-temperature UV/Vis-DRS (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0005">5b</a>), illustrating that the characteristic absorption band of IVCT remained observable within the range of 800–1100 nm at −60 °C. This indicates that IVCT within V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA can be accessed with minimal thermal activation energy. Moreover, as temperature increases, both broadening of the characteristic absorption band and enhancement in peak intensity are noted. Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0005">5c</a> further elucidates how IVCT synergistically enhances cycling stability and kinetics of electrochemical reactions by introducing V<sup>3+</sup> to activate previously blocked IVCT in MnPBA, thereby achieving electronic tuning of MnPBA alongside coupled electrochemical behavior and a mitigated Jahn–Teller effect under high voltage. The electron localization function (ELF) calculation results indicate that V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA possesses a more delocalized electron system along with enhanced intrinsic conductivity and rapid Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion, synergistically optimizing the kinetics of electrochemical reactions and resulting in remarkable rate performance.
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="anie202500254-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/b4f77bc0-cb1e-406c-a57d-9d8027f05c87/anie202500254-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/b4f77bc0-cb1e-406c-a57d-9d8027f05c87/anie202500254-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/65f1e203-e506-4370-aece-4ef1642e0b16/anie202500254-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/b4f77bc0-cb1e-406c-a57d-9d8027f05c87/anie202500254-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=anie202500254-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fanie.202500254" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>a) Electron transfer diagram of IVCT. b) Intensity contour maps of in situ variable-temperature UV/Vis-DRS. c) Mechanism of IVCT co-enhancing battery cycling reversibility and electrochemical kinetics.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>To investigate the practical applicability of V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA, we systematically assembled sodium-ion full cells utilizing V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA as the cathode and hard carbon (HC) as the anode (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0006">6a</a>). The performance of the V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA//HC full cell was evaluated for comparative analysis. Based on CV and charge/discharge curves of both electrodes (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0006">6b</a>), the operational voltage window for the full cell was established at 1.0–4.0 V. Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0006">6c</a>-6e illustrates the galvanostatic charge−discharge curves, rate performance, and cycling life of the full cell. The cell exhibits a reversible specific capacity of 126.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup> (based on the cathode) with an average operating voltage of 2.87 V, corresponding to a high energy density of 280.5 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> based on the total mass of positive and negative electrodes. Moreover, V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA//HC full cell delivers admirable discharge capacities of 126.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup> and 71.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> even at 1000 mA g<sup>−1</sup> (based on the cathode). By contrast, the MnPBA//HC full cell delivers disappointing discharge capacities of 31.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>. The long-term cycling performance of V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA//HC full cell is displayed in Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0006">6e</a>, demonstrating respectable capacity retentions of 85 % after 100 cycles at 100 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, and the comparative MnPBA//HC full cell demonstrates only a capacity retention of 59 %. An electric fan with a power of 1.8 W and LED light sets can be successfully driven by the V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA//HC pouch cell (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0006">6e</a> and Figure S35). We further tested the wide temperature performance of V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA in the range from −50 to 60 °C to provide potential relevant to the practical application. At −15 °C, the superior rate capability of V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA with reversible capacities of 121.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup> and 51.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 1000 mA g<sup>−1</sup> is further demonstrated in Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0006">6f</a> and Figure S32. Encouragingly, under a current density of 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, the V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA could deliver 151, 123, 102, 75, and 65 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> initial specific capacity at 60, 30, −15, −30 and −50 °C, respectively (Figure <a href="#anie202500254-fig-0006">6g</a> and Figure S36, S37). V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA still demonstrates enhanced electrochemical kinetics and superior working stability than that of MnPBA under low temperatures.
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="anie202500254-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/1d367198-8323-47e5-a588-3da9dffd164b/anie202500254-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/1d367198-8323-47e5-a588-3da9dffd164b/anie202500254-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/bf1b2b9f-0a42-4a56-aff7-5ff92477e8d0/anie202500254-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/1d367198-8323-47e5-a588-3da9dffd164b/anie202500254-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=anie202500254-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fanie.202500254" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>Schematic diagram of the V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PB//hard carbon full cell. b) CV and charge−discharge curves of the V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PB cathode and HC anode. c) Galvanostatic charge−discharge curves, d) rate capability of the full cell, and (e) cycling performance. f) rate performance of MnPBA and V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA at −15 °C. g) cycling performance at 60, 30, −15, −30, −50 °C of MnPBA and V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="anie202500254-sec-0003">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="anie202500254-sec-0003-title"> Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, Intervalence Charge Transfer (IVCT) of manganese and iron to vanadium ions is unraveled in a series of novel V<sup>3+</sup>-substituted manganese-based Prussian blue analogues (MnPBA) for enhancing the reversibility and kinetics of electrochemical reactions. IVCT occurs between Mn<sup>2+</sup> and V<sup>3+</sup>, as well as Fe<sup>2+</sup> and V<sup>3+</sup>, reducing the electronic band gap and Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion barrier for rapid electron and Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion. Besides, the sites with different formal charges undergo electronic coupling, rendering the coupling of a charge–discharge platform. More importantly, the IVCT between Mn<sup>3+</sup>-V<sup>4+</sup> transfers the single electron on Mn<sup>3+</sup> e<sub>g</sub> orbital under high voltage, mitigating its strong Jahn–Teller distortion. Consequently, coupled electrochemical behavior combined with an inhibited Jahn–Teller effect synergistically enhances its electrochemical performance, endowing the V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA electrode with outstanding cycling stability (91.6 % capacity retention after 300 cycles at 20 mA g<sup>−1</sup>) and exceptional high-rate capability (136.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 20 mA g<sup>−1</sup> and 94.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 20 A g<sup>−1</sup>). In situ XRD indicates that V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA material exhibits a quasi-zero-strain behavior during the Na<sup>+</sup> insertion and extraction&nbsp;processes. The fast electrode kinetics are confirmed by the GITT, CV, and in situ DRT measurements. Notably, the IVCT mechanism is exposed by comprehensive&nbsp;ex situ XPS characterizations. Moreover, the prototype sodium-ion full cells assembled by the V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA cathode and HC anode display bright application prospects. Finally, the V<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>PBA cathode demonstrates impressive discharge capacity and cycling stability across a temperature range of −50 to 60 °C. This study offers new insights into electronically tuning the PBA cathode for high-performance SIBs, leveraging its unique electronic conductivity and synthetic flexibility.</p>
         </section>
